<Text>For the Jai Jadat event at the Bakersfield College Theater. It was my first time and it was Awesome. I was told by a regular that the theater had been renovated and the results were beautiful. The acoustics were aided by what appears to be bamboo panels hung from the ceiling and the drapes were a soft green; a total departure from the expected dark red. The performance from a talented group of young people and children from India on their first trip anywhere in the world was nothing short of astonishing. A celebration of M. K. Gandhi's 150th birthday and a recognition of many people past and present who stood for the idea of Peace on Earth. I'll be sure to return for future events!< /Text><Resp>None<//Resp><date>1557865066408< /date></record>

<Text>Top Wok disappointed me. I was craving the Chinese take-out comfort food I remember from my youth--not fancy fusion cuisine, not challenging authentic cuisine, and not fast food--and after reading these reviews, I was hopeful that Top Wok would hit the spot. I ordered hot braised shrimp and pork with broccoli. The pork was not great, but the shrimp was the real disaster. There were two shrimp in my hot braised shrimp. Two. The dish was 80% under-cooked carrots. If they were out of shrimp, they could have told me and I would have ordered something else.

< name>
Amy Kitchen<//name>
<time>1531665934849</time>< Rating>
5< /Rating>
< text>
Los Angeles and the surrounding cities are peppered with stellar restaurants that are hidden except to the locals that found them.  In a little strip mall in Redondo Beach lives one of those hidden gems:  Top Wok!

This is the Chinese food you are always hoping to be served.  It sets the bar high for anything else you will find in Socal, whether super high end or hole in the wall.  We live an hour away and drive to Redondo Beach just to eat here.

Potstickers that are delicate and delicious.  Beef sticks that I could eat as a meal by themselves.  The sole in hot garlic sauce and shrimp in black bean sauce and both savory and chock full of tender bits of fish/shrimp and fresh veggies.  My personal favorite is the Kung Pao (we got the chicken) - honestly every time we go out for Chinese, this is the Kung Pao we are always comparing to!!

No steam table.  Cooked to order.  SO worth the drive.  Seriously, there should be a line down the street.  So damn good!!</text>

<Rate>5<//Rate>< Text>
Excellent food excellent prices-Im pretty picky about where I eat especially when it comes to Oriental food. This place is amazing I cannot figure out how they can serve big portions of home cooked food at these very good prices. The beef is sourced from Australia, the noodles and vegetables are fresh, it is the opposite of typical oriental fare whose commercial pre-fab ingredients make everything taste the same; or worse, taste flat like a Pik up Stix or other unimaginative chain. I have had the Chicken curry, sweet and sour, and my favorite the Kung Pao chicken. None disappoint; fresh, home cooked and cheap. I eat there whenever Im in the area, good thing i dont live in Redondo or Id be there everyday, fat as a sumo wrestler.<//Text>

< review>
These guys are awesome!! I've been here twice and always left with a smile. They are super knowledgeable and honest. The first diagnosis was spot on and gave me peace of mind, but included a warning that there was a strong possibility that one or more of my injectors was returning too much fuel, causing my truck to go into limp mode from low fuel rail pressure while under heavy load. I finally pulled the trigger on having them pull and test the injectors, after all it has 350,000 miles on it. Testing confirmed the initial diagnosis so they installed new injectors and repaired a leaking coolant line to the turbo which again gives me peace of mind that I am good to tow my trailer to the Sierras without worrying about failures. I have every confidence in recommending them to any diesel owner that needs top notch mechanical work done by honest people that won't take advantage like so many diesel shops do. They will take the time to explain things in such a way that you will feel comfortable making an educated decision. This is the only shop that will ever see my truck for any mechanical issues! I wish I could give them 10 stars!!!
Update: I was preparing for the Sierra trip I mentioned when I noticed a spot of coolant under the truck. I called Donovan and he told me to bring it in and he would check it out. I figured it was something related to the hose that they had fixed, which they didn't charge me for and his tech probably spent 2 hours on it. It turned out that my water pump was starting to leak, not bad yet and there was absolutely no pressure to replace it, but being the good guy that he is, Donovan ordered the parts and got it done for me as quickly as he could to ensure that I could take my trip to the Sierras without the threat of losing my cooling system 300 miles away from home. I got back this weekend from the Sierras and the truck ran amazing! < Text>
Afters is super amazing. I love how they can get the donut to be as hot as it is while still having the ice cream be really really cold inside. I always think that I'll be breaking my teeth while eating these milky buns but it turns out okay each time.

My favorite flavor is hands down, the cookie butter. Very similar to my overall favorite flavor, salted caramel, the cookie butter is sweet and savory. It goes really well with the milky bun which is also sweet. Their cookie monster flavor is also really good.

I've never been disappointed with this place. I think the milky buns are a much better version of what everyone's trying to do with ice cream fusions, like with cookies. They have so many flavors and they're patient with you trying the ones you find hitting your curiosity.

The staff is always quite friendly making Afters on the higher end of ice cream parlors out there. I always recommend this place to all my friends and you should definitely check it out.<//Text>

< text>
The location is easy to miss since the signage is minimal, but trust me, you don't want to miss it. There are some really interesting ice cream concoctions like the blue cookie monster flavor with cookie pieces in it (their most popular flavor) or the peanut butter s'mores flavor, which I tried. I had my ice cream in a glazed milky bun, which tasted essentially like having my ice cream in a warm glazed doughnut. The soft, warm, sweet bun surrounded cold, creamy ice cream with crunchy pretzel pieces in it. SO GOOD! The store is pretty plain and doesn't have much ambiance, but if you're looking for a unique treat, this is the place to go.<//text>

< rating>
3</rating>
< Review>
Tried the very hyped up "milky bun-" a glazed donut with ice cream. Although it is a unique dessert, overall for me it was too much sugar overload.

I went on a Sunday afternoon and the wait was about 25 minutes to get to try the ice cream. The decor is hip, sarcastic, and overall just very hipster.

They have a variety of interesting flavors and mixes: for the milky bun you get to choose a topping and they mix it with the ice cream and put it in a warm donut. The best ice cream I tried was jasmine tea- very refreshing and delicious. I instead got cookie butter with captain crunch because I thought the textures would go well.

$5 for this dessert is a little much for me, I'd rather have a cookie ice cream sandwich for half the price. Because of the price and wait, I think the Milky Bun isn't really worth it.</Review>

<Rate>5</Rate>< Text>
I found out about this place on Instagram! A friend of mine made me drool on my phone after she waited hours in line for a milky bun and posted pictures.

Lucky for me I was traveling back to Cali anyway and had to add this on my list to try!  A local in town said to come early to beat the crowd, yes sir.

The biz sign is on the window made difficult to find unless you have really good eyes ha it just says ice cream in small letters on building, but let me save you the trouble it's sandwiched between a Chinese restaurant chain(forgot name!) and Hallmark in the left corner of the plaza.

They have a list of original ice cream names you won't find anywhere that I can think of,  had trouble deciding, wanted to try them all, ended up with my favorites and I knew I can't go wrong with the flavors. Fun and cool toppings to add.

Glazed Milky Bun + Salted Caramel + Cookie Butter + a sprinkle of lucky charms= sweet warm buttery orgasmic milky bang goodness!!!!

Then you feel like going for a walk after that, but totally worth getting fat for! :)

I'm coming back to try the churro and Vietnamese coffee ice cream!!!< /Text>

< name>
Hanae K</name>
< time>
1425872341581<//time>
<Text>The Hype: The glazed milky bun, which is a donut.

The Yum: Their ice cream quality is top notch. I really love their creative flavors such as the cookie monster, churro ice cream, viet coffee, etc.

Jasmine Milk Tea ice cream: I do recommend it. It's not too sugary and it's not super rich.

The Line: It wasn't that long and it gave me time to read some yelp reviews to see what to get.

Tips:
If you still want the milky bun with ice cream then get it without the glaze. The glaze will stick to the paper wrap and the sugar will take over the ice cream flavor. My head hurts from the sugar high I got from it.

If you want the milky bun sealed or filled, they will warm up the bun so your ice cream will melt faster.

Best to get just the ice cream... unless this is your first time here then it doesn't hurt to get the bun so you can cross it off your foodie-list.</Text><gmapID>0x80dd27390c3fe7ab:0x98c5e2648edf90f4</gmapID>< Response>

< Review>
Came here one Sunday afternoon and was surprised to find a line outside of the shop! I debated not waiting but figured why not? In the 45 min line, my sister, parents and myself all decided that we wanted to try the glazed milky bun ($5) with different ice creams.

For $5, you can get the bun (glazed or non-glazed) with ice cream in the middle and one topping. They had a pretty good variety of flavors and toppings to choose from.

I personally had the churro bun with oreo bits but also sampled the below:

-cookie monster
-strawberry
-cookie butter

All of them were really really delicious. It was hard to distinguish the exact quality of the ice cream because it was overwhelmed by the taste of the glazed donut. That being said - the overall combo was sweet, messy goodness and I did enjoy the churro flavor.

Not sure if I would wait in that line again but I'd definitely come back again if I'm in the area.< /Review>

Wow! Does Afters live up to the hype? Man I want to find something bad to say about this place but I just can't.  This is one of the few times that the hype actually panned out. Most of the time hype is just a bunch of people following each other for no reason. Afters is worth it! Waiting in line for an hour is not for me. I have only waited 10 or 15 minutes each time. Any more than that and I will pass. For anyone that hates waiting, don't be "that guy" who holds up the line by trying 10 samples. Yes you know who you are you and your cheap friends. I say 1 to 3 samples is fair game but think about what you want while you are in line instead of just pretend you are there for the first time and there isn't a line of impatient people behind you.

It's all about the ice cream. I have only been here a few times but I think the ice cream alone is worth it. I highly recommend getting the ice cream within a milky bun. I always go without toppings because I can go without the sugar adding to more sugar. Besides as my friend always says it's bikini season. I don't personally wear a bikini but I support those who do. I put Afters on my list of things I will make an exception for not eating healthy. I will always have some room for ice cream. Just eat healthy and exercise when you are not enjoying ice cream. <Date>1409183500760</Date>< Review>
DONUT + ICE CREAM = $$$$

Throughout the years I'm constantly seeing new and hyped up creations from the ramen burger to the cronut. I mean the idea is great and all but I think these things are seriously overhyped and unfortunately the same goes for the Milky Buns at Afters.

When I heard the line for Afters averages 45mins -1 hr long I knew it probably wouldn't be worth the wait. I had friends tell me about this place and show me pictures of the famous Milky Buns so being a foodie i knew i had to try it for myself. Luckily, this past weekend Jen H. and I dropped by after the Color Run around 2pm on Saturday and to our surprise there was no line! We waited about 5 minutes! So if you want to try this place I highly suggest coming here in the afternoon to avoid the crazy teens that gather here at night.

In terms of the dessert itself, I thought the handmade ice cream was delicious. I sampled a couple flavors and fell in love with the Acai blueberry because I love fruity flavors. The Milky Bun comes with one topping for around $5. I got fruity pebbles and it gave the Milky Bun ice cream sandwich a nice crunch and paired very well with the ice cream. As a whole, the Milky Bun tasted just like a donut ice cream sandwich. Imagine if you were to add really good ice cream inside a glazed donut then you would get the Milky Bun. There really isn't much to it then that so hype or no hype if you must try come during the off hours because the wait is ridiculous if you come at night.<//Review>

<userid>109815267831202318650< /userid>< Name>
Walter Macalma< /Name>
<time>1439241376896< /time><Rating>4</Rating>< Text>
Disclaimer: In depth review lies ahead.

Long has the tradition been the dessert come post meal, but years ago I met a man who was so in love with his dessert that he ate it first, knowing that if he were to get full and unable to finish his meal the 1 thing he wasn't going to miss was dessert so he would also often skip appetizers. It's on that premise that I think the name After's plays on, because I think the same effect would occur if they called it "And then".

Todays social media has changed the game in how we market. Beyond the website it's FB, IG, Vine and Twitter that are making the biggest strides. I actually think that the website is a little light on the features.  it's nice and all, fancy and bright, but not really intuitive or informative, just heavy on the pictures, links and promotion. I found out about Afters through IG and not Yelp or friends, that's a first since I'm obviously pretty active yelp hunter.

The signage is really just remnants and a little sketchy compared to the work they put in online. The seating is not tended to or cleaned as often as they are pushing out product. The parking lot is littered, literally with wrappers, melted ice cream and just junk. It looks like a parking lot after a sporting event. They need WAY more trash cans, more tables would be nice too, but not necessary. I don't mind coming here and eating here, but this isn't Starbucks where you set up your laptop and do HW, it's busy, it's packed and hanging around is wasting space when you see how many people want this stuff. D√©cor inside is stark and basic, 2 toned paint and I get the current Gucci mane reference, but it's kind of permanent for someone who has an expiration date on relevance. Maybe put that 1 in chalk or on a monitor versus paint. Wait can be up to an hour.

I LOVE the monthly changing menu. Check the website with progressive flavors like Milk & Cereal (though I never added sugar to my cereal I know some kids growing up who did, I think it's a regional or cultural thing). Smooth, not too rich, unique. Vietnamese Coffee is  bold up front, but doesn't linger and isn't highly caffeinated like the coffee itself.  Churro is a little gritty and is excellent with caramel as I try to go for the dulce de leche end note. Jasmin Milk tea is a good replica of the typical milk tea you get from boba spots, but since it's ice cream it's quite a bit thicker. Almond cookie is liquid macaroons and great when you get it alone, no toppings. Cookie Monster to me was a bit of a bust. Their rocky road could use more nuts and marshmallows.

It would be nice to have fresh pressed waffle cones and standard made upon ordering. Many of their flavors are so rich you almost need something to mellow them out or go no toppings and in a cup, not cone. NOW onto the star of the show the Milky Bun which is basically a donut, sliced in half, stuffed with your choice of ice cream and toppings and resealed. There are large variences in workmanship as I've had picturesque and then abominations made. The glazed even when eaten right away is messy so go plain and no toppings is my preference. You really can't eat just one, so why wait in line all that time to realize it. Buy 2 and don't be disappointed.

I like the concept, and the ice cream, marketing is on point, but using an old Mexican food shop in a shopping center that probably couldn't handle you popularity or need for immediate expansion lacked some foresight. Oh the curse of innovation. It's a great place to come eat after you get  G Burger across the parking lot. Warning: I've seen 2 people be distracted and hit pedestrians here. Parking lot is dangerous so don't' be distracted walking or driving. My guess is you'll see flavored buns here soon. May your ice cream be high and fat and your buns always be milky.<//Text>

<rate>4<//rate><Text>I may never have found out about this place if not for my good friends at Bobalife, (if you love all things boba/cutesy/Asian, I suggest you look them up), and when you have an endorsement by 2 people who clearly know their sweets, you bet I'm going to drive an hour to try these ice cream-stuffed milky buns.

First off, I have to strongly urge you to show up at least 15 minutes before they open, as the lines get hella long, and they stay that way indefinitely. Secondly, these guys have some really unique & delicious ice cream flavors on the menu, so you'll want to bring a friend or two to split a couple of milky buns/ice cream cups. Lastly, bring your appetite; ice cream wedged in between a big glazed donut = sweets overload.

All that being said, who doesn't love the idea of an ice cream sandwich made with a gorgeous piece of sweetly fried Heaven that is the Milky Bun? It's fairly simply: You decide whether or not you want the ice cream in a milky bun, (and why wouldn't you?). You choose your flavor. You add a topping. You pay. You go outside, and try to find a secluded area where you can stuff your face, as the delicious, messy ice cream runs down your fingers. Repeat, if necessary.
With the smorgasbord of flavors like, Churro, Cookie Butter, Vietnamese Coffee, & Jasmine Milk Tea, and toppings like Cap'n Crunch cereal & chocolate chips, you'll want to use the time spent in line to plan your order to waste as little time as possible. Once you're there, you're a bit pressured to move quickly.
Want my advice? Try the most popular combinations of a glazed milky bun with cookie butter, topped with Cap'n Crunch cereal. Or if you're feeling like some java, go for the Vietnamese Coffee topped with some chocolate chips.

Just don't do what I did, show up alone, and then decide to get two stuffed milky buns and scarf them down at the same time. I'm still recovering from the food coma.<//Text><pictures>None< /pictures><Resp>None<//Resp>< GmapID>

<name>Rodney S< /name><response>None<//response><time>1415650200023</time><Rate>4</Rate><UserId.>102918253898437847981<//UserId.>< Text>
"So I sing you to sleep, after the lovin." - "After the Lovin", Englebert Humperdinck

I first heard of AFTERS Handcrafted Ice Cream during a segment on the KTLA Morning News, featuring their trademark "Milky Buns" & their variety of unique flavors.  I knew right away that I had to move my hot ass on over there someday, and with plans on having dinner at the nearby Shin Sen Gumi Robata & Yakitori, it was the perfect opportunity to come in & and see what all the fuss was about.

AFTERS is located on Brookhurst & Talbert, in Fountain Valley.  If you're looking for a big AFTERS sign, you're SOL.  Just look for ICE CREAM on the left of the plaza, and you've found it.

The friendly employees will kindly let you sample whatever you like.

Around 6pm on a Monday night, with only a few people in line.  Perfect timing by yours truly.

Donuts aren't really my thing, so I already had in mind to have strictly ice cream.  I refer to donuts as "heart attack food".  One of the most unhealthiest things to eat.  I already imagine a "Milky Bun" to be way too sweet for me, so I can share my own unbiased opinion on the "coup de grace" of any ice cream parlor - the ice cream!

Of all that I tried, my favorites were the churro, milk & cereal, jasmine milk tea & Vietnamese coffee.

Each had the distinct flavor of their namesakes.  I loved the crunch of the Frosted Flakes in the milk & cereal.  All had great creamy texture that good ice cream should have.

Service was good.  The employees didn't hesitate to let me sample whatever I'd like.  There are a few outdoor tables to sit & enjoy your ice cream.  Parking is in private lot.

AFTERS Handcrafted Ice Cream makes high quality ice cream in a unique assortment of fun flavors.  I don't think I'd go out of my way to return for more ice cream, but if I'm in the area, I definitely see myself diving in for another scoop or 4 ;p

Highly recommend!
NOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNOM<//Text>
